Pilot interview 
Figure 13:Research Process 
==PAGE:51==
 
40 
 
barriers prevent them from being data-driven decision-making, which is the aim of this study to 
find them and generate a framework to improve them. 
Data gathering is the critical step of this research, and it was performed by a set of face-to-
face interviews with ten (10) different key decision-makers who can use DDDM practices in their 
daily activities. The interviewees were selected based on their position as important decision-
makers such as managers or heads of departments. 
 The interviews typically lasted 45 to 60 minutes, were audio-recorded and transcribed, and 
inserted in the analysis software. To prevented misinterpretation, all interviews were recorded with 
a voice recorder under the permission of interviewees. Then the transcripts have been sent for the 
interviewees to confirm them. Moreover, for privacy reasons, the identity of the interviewees was 
not included in this study. 
This study relies on a qualitative approach, with each interviewee's ideas and opinions 
being considered and tested for outcomes, findings, and recommendations. The interviews' 
outcomes will then review using the design science methodology to prepare a list of statements 
and recommendations and generate a final solution as a framework for implementing data-driven 
decision-making. 
3.3 Questioner Design and Interviewees Profiles 
The interview questions are designed based on the identified dimensions from the literature 
and pilot meetings with the analytics and insights team manager (see Appendix 3: Interview 
Questions).  As illustrated in Table 4, the main four dimensions are Data, Process, Implementation, 
and People, and the sub-elements directly impact them. 
The interview questions were designed based on these dimensions and elements to identify 
the current situation of the Danfoss-climate solution department in decision-making processes and 
find the barriers for implementing a DDDM. For each dimension, four (4) to five (5) questions are 
provided. They were open questions that the interviewees answered in their own words, and there 
are no predefined answers (Johannsesson and Perjons 2014).

3.4 Data Analysis 
After the interviews were conducted, transcribed, and confirmed by the interviewees, they 
needed to be categorized. The collected data was analyzed by using the Maxqda software (See 
Appendix 4: Maxqda Screenshot). This software assists in structuring and coding the qualitative 
data. The codes are defined based on the identified dimension listed in Table 4. Therefore, the 
approach of the analysis is deductive. 
Additionally, if any new aspects mentioned in the interviews are not already in the model 
and would be worth adding, they will be the inductive findings of the analysis. Thus, the final 
solution is a framework produced based on literature and empirical data analysis findings.  
 
 
 
 
==PAGE:55==
 
44 
 
CHAPTER 4 
 4 Data analysis 
CHAPTER INTRODUCTION 
In this chapter, the analysis of the collected data through 10 interviews will be presented. 
The approach is based on empirical analysis. The chapter consists of: Section 4.1 How data 
analysis; Section 4.2 Summary of the overall data analysis. 
 
4.1 Data analysis 
4.1.1 Data 
The first dimension has four main sub-elements: strategy, resources, Technology doption, 
and monitoring and controlling data. The main focus of the interview in each element are: 
• Strategy: Is there any alignment between strategy and the collected data? 
• Resources: what are the primary resources for collecting data? 
• Technology adoption: what is the main problem for technology adoption for users 
of the system? 
• Monitoring and controlling of data: Is there any feedback system on the data 
lifecycle? 
4.1.1.1 Strategy 
 Identifying the business goal will help organizations evaluate the amount of funding or 
staff needed for the initiative. It is essential to have a strategic vision to know what kind of data to 
collect for any future improvement or project analysis. Interviewees approve that having a strategy 
==PAGE:56==
 
45 
 
for collecting data depends on the projects and decisions that decision-makers are involved in 
based on their positions and the demands and needs of the departments. Danfoss has a position 
responsible for finding out what kind of data is needed to be collected. Head Of Business 
Intelligence stated it is a part of his responsibility:  
“… my part of the job is also exactly to share the proposals with the top management as 
well, how can we leverage our data. And then of course, naturally, then how do we collect it. Do 
we have the budget on the resources side and all these kinds of planning, and so on, and then 
translating that into the technology…” 
It was discovered from the interviews that the lack of access to data leads to perform 
intuition-based decisions. If the decision-makers have to make structured decisions, they know the 
process and have experience in that area, so they have already collected many data and have a clear 
plan for data.  However, when they need to perform unstructured decision-making, they need to 
find out what data is available. As the young strategic director stated:  
“…When we go into something completely new. And we have no experience where we are 
not today, then we are struggling a bit more to say okay, what is our plan for data, we then say 
okay we need to get a fact pack, we have this process when we run strategy projects where we say 
okay, first we need to get the effect package in place and then you can start building on your 
strategy, and then we work on that right and then we say, our plan is now to work for a month. To 
build our effect” 
  
Some interviewees stated they have a road map for what they need as data for their 
decision-making processes, but they are still not good enough in this area.  However, a good data 
strategy needs to clarify how to collect data, share it, and make access for others to use it. In 
addition, they should align with business or project strategies to grow the company data assets. 
During the analysis of the results, all the interviewees have this experience looking for specific 
data, and sometimes it is not produced. In addition, sometimes, they do not have access to the data, 
and it takes time to find the data. For example, the Head of Service Solution Development stated:  
“..definitely especially sales data from our ERP systems. It's not something that they use, 
that they use on a day to day basis, But every now and then I do need access to the sales data. And 
this where I rely on our BI teams and sales teams that, that are working on a day to day basis, with, 
with sales data” 
==PAGE:57==
 
46 
 
Sometimes they have the strategy, but they do not know how to collect the data. The Head 
of Product Management Digital Services stated: 
“There is strategy based on the needs of the customer but they still dont know how to collect 
the data from end user.”

4.1.1.2 Resources 
The data is categorized as structured and unstructured data. Both categories are used in 
Danfoss depends on the position and the responsibility. The resource of collecting of these data is 
different. Most of the data is collected with IoT sensors, CRM, and some data collecting by 
outsourcing. The young Business Development Manager had experience looking for data that does 
not exist anymore. Therefore, they outsource it to a research institute to collect that data: 
“we would like to know something about a new magazine where we where we don't have 
anything to say and then we are contacting a research institute and then we have to explain them 
what, what is the data we, we are looking for. And then they are trying to make a proposal of how 
they want to collect the data, how they want to present the data and stuff like that and then we will 
say, Yeah, this is exactly what we are looking for, so please go out and how can you generate the 
data and then send the report to us.”

4.1.1.3 Technology Adoption 
 
Based on the interviews, the essential facts in technology adoption are in three critical 
concepts: Data availability, Trust, and data quality. 
Data availability  
Based on the literature review in section 2.4 Data-driven decision-making approaches, Data 
availability is one of the vital Data governance capabilities factors for implementing a DDDM.  
The interviews showed that the decision-makers check the availability of related data based on the 
project. They used an analytic forum and meeting to know what kind of data is available in the 
system and workshop for learning new BI tools. However, not everybody joining every meeting. 
For example, the Analytics & Insights Manager stated:  
“when we start projects and we look at data available, and idea, then where do we have 
data available, or what what does it take to get the data and to have data available and also 
have it in the right quality. Yeah, so whether we call the workshops or meetings, then, then yes, 
that's, that's part of the process when we start up a new project” 
  
They also confirmed that these meetings were based on the current project and did not have 
regular meetings about the available data in the whole system. Six of them confirmed that these 
meetings are for the people who are involved in the project; it is not for all people of Danfoss. 
Customer Experience Manager stated: 
“ we don't have a regular review of if there are more information sources” 
 The interviews also discovered that the interviewees do the repetitive data creation process 
in a different department, which wasted time. The reason for this issue is that the departments do 
not have a relationship. They referred to this problem as the lack of integration in the system. With 
an integrated system, they avoid this kind of process of data creation. Head of service innovation 
stated: 
“There might be others that have some pieces of the puzzle of the data person, but it's just 
invisible to me because I don't know it's there” 
Table 8: Elements and Sub elements of technical adoption: data availability 
Main dimension 
Elements 
sub-elements 
Technical

 Trust 
  
The biggest concerns of the interviewees are Trust in data. They knew that the company 
would switch to data-driven approaches, investigate buying technologies, and implement data-
driven system steps. However, they preferred to make their decision based on their experienced, 
and the reason was they do not trust in data.  They used data as support for their daily activities 
and decision-making. The reasons are different. Head of Service Solution Development does not 
have 100% trust in the data. He stated: 
“ No ,because in a company like Danfoss that's been collecting data for the past 40 years. 
A lot of data cleansing has to be done. “ 
The analysis of the interviews showed that lack of trust was due to a lack of knowledge about data 
generation and doubted in the analysis of the reports. Vice President Product Development and 
Supply Chain stated: 
“if I trust the way they generated the data good enough, I have to go with that.”

Data quality 
The main reason for asking people how to improve the quality of data was to determine the 
weaknesses of the current system, the main important area for improvement from their aspects. 
The answers were interesting. This study found that the mindset as a fundamental needed to be 
fixed. Because if every people involved in the implementation of Data-driven culture in the 
company should know if they do not retain the correct data, this affects the data quality.  If the 
==PAGE:60==

input data is incomplete and inaccurate, the resulting output is unreliable, lacks practical value, 
and leads to untrusting data. The strategy director and Head Of Business Intelligence stated: 
“ It is garbage in garbage out “ 
The Analytics & Insights Manager recommenced that improving the architecture and data 
management could help people access more reliable and meaningful data. The Analytics & Insights 
Manager stated: 
“All the way from defining common data model, how do we cleaning data, normalize data 
so what's usable, how do we structure in a way which is meaningful. So having the right metadata 
and right source system” 
There were many needs for integrating all systems to handle data correctly using 
technology to ensure it contains updated data on the system. It was noticed that some interviewees 
need external data such as GDP, PMI…. . This could be an area that should be considered in data 
strategy. 
The interviewees stated that it is also essential to the training of the people to have a 
consistent approach to understanding that there are different kinds of data and learn how to import 
them correctly into the system, analyze them by using the correct analyzing method, and finally, 
how to use it.

4.1.1.4 Monitoring and controlling of data 
As mentioned in the above section, Danfoss people need better data to trust. Therefore, the 
most crucial question could be: Is there any strategy for improving the data quality?   
==PAGE:61==
 
50 
 
Based on the literature, one way to improve users based on their needs is to implement a 
feedback system. Three of the interviewees agreed that they have a feedback system on data. These 
people were from departments where the basic of the department was data-driven such as strategy, 
finance, and business. Therefore, they need to discuss the quality of data and in their routine 
meetings. They have these feedback systems on their own created information for their reports. 
For example, the business development manager stated:  
“ …I've been working with our workshop in a half a year and here we are also building, 
for example, a dashboard that is saying something about how good is the product data in the web 
shop…we have set up dashboards to measure how good are we in data quality before we can take 
the next steps in functional web shop.” 
Three of them agreed that the feedback on data quality is not structured; it is based on the 
data cleaning activity and the foundation for analysis. For example, the customer experience 
manager stated: 
“we have data quality improvement areas in Danfoss, but, it's not too often that I am doing 
it in a structured way that I improve data, I'm just flagging Hey there is something wrong, or it 
looks like in my understanding this needs to be different than I can flag it” 
This study found that if the data was presented in a way that the other people could 
understand the reason for using the data, they could challenge it. This makes an automatic loop of 
feedback on the data quality and the reports. It depends on the data mindset that people to be data-
driven. If their perception of data is considered an essential asset for their daily activities, they 
would feel more responsible for data quality. They will challenge it to obtain high-quality data. 
The strategy director stated:  
“ I think it's more it's up to, again, this mindset, you know, data is important to, challenge, 
and you have to present that and you have to present the challenges with the data, so they know it 
so they are informed and they can make a conscious decision “

4.1.2 Process 
The process is one of the crucial backbones of implementing data-driven decision-making. 
Based on the assumptions, Danfoss has the foundation of a data-driven platform. Therefore, 
analyzing the current decision-making process and finding the barriers to applying the data-driven 
approaches in decision-making could help achieve the goal of this study. Based on the interviews, 
the focus of analysis of the process is on decision making approaches. Hence, the process is spilites 
into these topics: 
• What is the most common approach to decision-making in Danfoss? 
• What is the most critical lack of data-driven decision-making in Danfoss? 
4.1.2.1 What is the most common approach to decision-making in Danfoss? 
When looking at how decisions were often made came down to the manager responsible 
for making decisions. Based on the availability of qualified data and how much the decision-
makers trust the data or their experiences, both gut feeling and data-driven approaches are used in 
Danfoss. It was discovered from the interviewees that decisions are mainly based on the intuition 
of the decision-makers and based on their feelings about expectations from the projects. The point 
is that gut feeling is involved in any decision-making. The Head of intelligence believed that the 
source of gut feeling is the knowledge that people could gain from experience or training. He 
stated: 
“ The only difference is that how much you separate the gut feeling to the data or the 
facts… I think it's always at the back of the mind there. Knowledge is defined by the gut feeling..” 
The finding from the interviews showed that Danfoss decision-makers used the data as a 
support for intuition decisions.  The other factor is time, which has a direct effect on decision 
approaches. The strategic director stated: 
“where you do not have data, then it will be intuition because it is the process of getting to 
data having the database is too long and they don't have the time to do that right. So I guess it 
depends a lot on that.” 
This study found it also depends on the size of the decision and its impact on the 
organization. For example, the business development manager stated that: 
 “ Big decision can be made purely on an intuition..” 
==PAGE:63==
 
52 
 
  
One of the interviewees stated that it also depends on the culture of the decision-makers. 
The individualism or collectivist culture made decision-makers trust the more agreed approach for 
decision making. Interviewees verify that the most common approach in Danfoss is intuition. 
Therefore, it makes sense to first change the mindset by trusting data with improving the data 
quality. The Head of Product Management Digital Services stated: 
“You know Denmark, right you know the culture a little bit so it is, very. Yeah, buy in from 
everybody getting everybody on board, and then making decisions. On the other hand, if you 
compare intuition to to data driven. I would also say it's more intuition.”.  
The most important factors which lead to intuition base decisions are listed in Table 12. 
Table 12: Elements and Sub elements for Process: Decision making: factors lead to an intuition-based 
decision 
Main dimension 
Elements 
sub-elements 
Making decision 
The most 
important 
factors lead to 
intuition 
decision 
• 
Untrust in data 
• 
Inequality and not inaccurate data 
• 
The size and the impact of the decision 
•

• 
The culture and the personality of the decision-maker 
To find the whole approach of decision making in Danfoss, the author asked the 
interviewees to consider a situation which is 50% of people who are involved in decision making 
are agree with the results of the data, and the other 50% prefer to use their intuition for making the 
last decision. Based on this hypothesis, it was discovered during the interviews that it is different 
based on the project and the approach of the meeting. First, the intuition decision-makers start to 
challenge the source of the data and the analysis. Then, they try to find a compromise between data 
and experience and fill the data gaps with experiences.  The Head of service innovation stated: 
“.. we try to find a compromise right So, and that is also due to the fact that in many cases, 
we have perhaps data that tell part of the story, and not the full story… So you have to fill in the 
blanks with experience,” 
They stated that they discuss, and if the empirical background of the data was not as 
expected, then the data is not trustable. The conclusion will be based on both approaches, but 
almost most of them agreed it is an intuition-based decision. The Head of service innovation stated: 
“ .. in many cases we're also at the point where we also acknowledge the fact that we cannot 
fully trust the data because the empirical background of the data is perhaps not always where we 
==PAGE:64==
 
53 
 
want it to be. So, that's usually at discussion point right and then the conclusion or where we end 
up is basically compromising and saying yes we can use the data for something, but we also have 
to trust our experience, and then we end up with a decision based on the combination of the two.” 
It was also discovered from some of the interviewees that data-driven decision-makers 
could convince the intuition decision-makers based on the facts and have strong arguments behind 
their data. Then, the experiment could fill the gaps in data. In that case, the decision will be based 
on data. The CFO stated:  
“ I think we can convince people with data, right, if, if we have data and they I mean 
assumption is also they trust the data that we are having, and they can see the same based on the 
data that we have in the line picture..” 
  
The most critical point in the above finding in this study was “trust.” If the people involved 
in the meeting trust generated data, the intuition decision-makers might overrule their stomach 
feeling. For example, the Vice President Product Development and Supply Chain stated: 
“I would challenge the data, try to, to get behind if there's any flaws in how they got the 
data or analyze the data, …I would need to be convinced to overrule my stomach feeling, if I trust 
the way they generated the data good enough, I have to go with that.. “ 
Another critical factor that the other interviewees mentioned was the fact pack. Suppose 
they have enough fact pack based on data. In that case, they will go through data-driven decision-
making; otherwise, if they do not have enough time to collect more data, they will baseline all their 
knowns ( data and experience) based on facts. They have confidence in their experience. Then, 
they will use the gut feeling for making the decision. The Head of business intelligence stated: 
“ we asked the team to determine more facts…the end of the day, then the question is, are 
we 100% fact base answer will be no, because they will look into an investigate. And there will be 
some knowns, which we can answer from data and there are some unknowns, which we can never 
answer from the data. And that's weird then, if we have knowns, with confidence, then we can talk 
about unknowns and then put our gut feeling that okay the baseline is good. Let's take this 
decision.”

4.1.2.2 What is the most critical lack of data-driven decision-making in Danfoss? 
One of the significant problems that decision-makers are involved in is better data 
governance, robust data management, and access to the relevant qualified data. They stated that 
they need access to qualified data that does not cost any effort to get them. All interviewees had 
the experience of looking for data or analysis for their decision-making. However, due to the 
limited time for the decision, they could not access correct data and reports. For example, the 
Customer Experience Manager stated:  
” Because I mean, that also if there for it is too big to get the data, then the effect of making 
the decision, then it doesn't make sense to get all those information right…. if it's too complicated 
to get, then we don't I wouldn't do it…” 
 It has also happened when a decision-maker must make an unstructured decision, they 
had data, but they do not have time for proper analysis. Therefore, they used to make intuition-
based decisions. For example, the Head of business intelligence stated: 
“in Unstructured decision, the problem is  time pressure normally due to a time pressure. 
We have data , but time is not enough to do a proper analysis” 
It is also essential that decision-makers understand the concept of the analysis that made 
the data, which means they need to hire skilled people or investigating for training the people and 
decision-makers based on their roles and needs to improve their analytics skills. It directly refers 
to the data literacy and interpretation skills of the decision-makers. The CFO and five other 
interviewees confirmed that : 
“I definitely think it will help us to make better decisions when we have better data…” 
“Improving the quality of data you could have better decision making processes... you need people 
that are good on the analysis part right and that are able to also first transform the data into 
something that you can use. So I think that's super important in the future...” 
“..availability of structured data.. and to learn how do we interpret the data and how do we 
actually act based on the data...” 
==PAGE:66==
 
55 
 
As illustrated in Table 14, it was also discovered from the interviews that the structure of 
the Danfoss organization as a hierarchical company made to be more route for decision making 
and the decision be top-down. Therefore, it limits the number of perspectives and the parameters 
when making the decisions. For example, the Head of Service Solution Development mentioned:  
“ Danfoss is still a hierarchical company, where many of the decisions are taken at the 
management level and this is something we're trying to change that,... This also limits the number 
of different perspectives you have in the decision making and the number of input parameters you 
can get when taking a decision … this would be the, basically the, the direction where we would 
improve “ 
Another factor was leadership. This study found that leading people towards data-driven 
approaches leads to growth in all levels of the company. For example, the Head of digitalization 
stated: 
“ I think that perspective, will be the challenge. The biggest challenge. I see. So the mindset 
change, is it takes a lot of time and also investment and commitment from the leadership and from 
different levels of the company to do that transition. “

4.1.3 Implementation 
Based on the assumption of this analysis, Danfoss already has implemented the data-driven 
approaches. In this dimension, the main goal is to define the benefit and challenges of the current 
==PAGE:67==
 
56 
 
system from the interviewees' aspects in implementing data-driven decision-making. Therefore, it 
consists of: 
• Is there any structure plan for knowledge sharing and training? 
• Is there any feedback or evaluation system to measure the outcomes of the decisions? 
• What are the benefit and challenges of implementing the DDDM?  
4.1.3.1 Is there any structure plan for knowledge sharing and training? 
This study found that they have different analytics forums, communities, and knowledge-
sharing systems in different departments. The point is that these platforms are more locally in each 
department or team, and there are not integrated perfectly. There were also some training 
workshops when new tools were developed. However, these trainings were held before they need 
to dig into it. Those who have an IT background and were responsible for developing the digital 
systems and tools stated that they have tools and meeting for training and following up for their 
teams. However, it is not in the standard form in other departments. For instance, the Vice President 
Product Development and Supply Chain stated: 
“ we do initial training, you know, everybody goes through the training to learn how does 
the system work…, Sometimes there's gaps of even once before they really need it. There's not 
enough follow up training. So the follow up training is not something that happens regularly so 
that so that is one element that can be improved on on this.” 
It is the same situation for knowledge sharing. When any department creates any new 
analysis tools or data, they do not have any platform to share it across the organization. The Head 
of Service Innovation stated: 
“ no, typically, typically not because typically we develop these,…. And, and we've not been 
proactively, let's say, reaching out and and telling everybody, only, let's say a few select people 
we've been involving and they are aware that this data is now available but not in a structured 
format so we don't have a, let's say, a platform, also to, to, to share the, the availability of data 
across the organization.”

4.1.3.2 Is there any feedback or evaluation system to measure the outcomes of the 
decisions? 
The reason for asking this question was to determine if there is any possibility of learning 
and motivating the decision-makers to learn from their experience using data in their decision-
making processes. The interviews showed that they define some KPIs for decisions to be met when 
they make their conclusions. However, from ten interviewees, just three of them were 90% sure 
that they evaluated the effectiveness of their decisions, which were from the finance and strategic 
department. The others stated that they have it but not in structure to control and monitor its journey 
and outcomes. For example, the Head of service innovation stated: 
“ I would say to certain extent, yes but again not in a very structured format so it's not it 
doesn't exist in a way where I can go back in three four or five six months in time or so and say 
which decisions that we make and what were the outcome. And now that we can see the result of 
those decisions.” 
 As listed in Table 16, it was discovered from the study that if they have a structure for 
tracking the impact of data-driven decision-making, it will help adjust the data-driven mindset and 
make it easy to accept the decisions based on data.

4.1.3.3 What are the benefit and challenges of implementing the DDDM? 
Challenges: 
This study found that most of the interviewees confirmed that decision-makers must know 
the data source and how data was produced. Therefore, transparency is an essential factor for 
qualified data for decision-makers to thoroughly understand the source of data and the analysis 
behind the data and analysis extraction. In addition, transparency will help decision-makers to trust 
data. The strategy director stated: 
“ Challenge is when the data itself is biased or not correctly understood this would have 
the opposite effect and lead to “blind decision making” and not questioning whether it is the 
correct decision. It could potentially also lead to reducing ownership of decision and instead 
“blaiming” the data” 
Misunderstanding of data may lead to wrong analysis methods or using incorrect data for 
their analysis. Training people based on their needs to data could help to avoid these issues. For 
example, the head of business intelligence stated: 
“the numbers were right, but they analyzed it wrongly which created the misunderstanding 
right”  
Changing the mindset of people from routine processes to new data-driven approaches 
takes time. It needs a structured plan for all levels of the organization, leading the decision-makers 
to trust the data and tools for their decision-making processes. The Vice President Product 
Development and Supply Chain stated: 
“ I see there is that people will, of course, shortcut places in order to get the work done 
and not, not fill out the right data or not fill the data in for everything and. And then, that's that's 
a risk for us to make database decisions, because then we don't have to be trusting, even some 
data which maybe is not correct.”

Benefit 
As shown in Table 18, all interviewees confirmed that the most crucial benefit of 
implementing DDDM approaches is that it covers the lack of data, process. This leads to having a 
unique mindset and increasing trust, commitment, collaboration, and making more qualified 
decisions in a shorter time. One of the interviewees' concerns was that making decisions is slow 
due to the lack of helpful information. The Vice President Product Development and Supply Chain 
stated: 
“ I find that we are slow in making decisions, and it's often because we don't have enough 
information, or we don't trust the information…. We're just delaying the process and making us 
less competitive “ 
Another factor was reviewing the processes based on the value getting out of them. Then 
the processes should be streamlined to allow others to use it and prevent repetitive analysis and 
wasting time. Thus, the technology could help to accelerate for implementation of intelligent 
processes for qualified decision making.  
As illustrated in Table 18, they all agreed that data-driven decision-making could help them 
make a competitive advantage and have obtained higher performance.

4.1.4 People 
Based on the theoretical background in literature and interview results, the decision-
makers' characteristics could impact their decision-making processes. Therefore, in this research, 
the focus is on three dimensions:  
▪ Data literacy skills 
▪ Personality characteristics of the decision-makers  
▪ Culture 
 
4.1.4.1 Data literacy 
Dykes in 2017 stated that for applying the data-driven approaches in any data-driven 
decision making, it is essential that decision-makers have a minimum standard of data analytics 
knowledge. (Dykes 2017). He discovered four essential dimensions: Data knowledge, Data 
assimilation, Data interpretation, and Data skepticism and curiosity. Furthermore, it was 
discovered from the interviews that all the interviewees are interested in data-driven reports even 
they did not have the related background education. For example, the Vice President Product 
Development and Supply Chain mentioned: 
“I love to read that report, even though it's not my day to day work… “  
As per discussions with the Head of intelligence and Analytics & Insights Manager, it was 
identified that they have some platforms such as forums and social networks on Teams or 
communities to train people for using the BI tools, but it is not in structure form. The Head of 
Service Solution Development mentioned:  
==PAGE:72==
 
61 
 
“ in Danfoss, something called a data analytics forum(meeting every Monday), where it's 
not only a manager level but in general for more. Most people dealing with data managers or 
individual contributors to share experiences, …. not everybody is joining every meeting… people 
decide what is of interest to them or not” 
This study found that training is essential for people to know how to use data for their 
analysis. Sometimes people used the wrong analysis method for analyzing the data. The head of 
intelligence mentioned: 
“in many times we have found out the people who were analyzing it, they analyzed it 
wrongly. So the numbers were right, but they analyzed it wrongly which created the 
misunderstanding … “ 
It was also recommended by most of the interviewees that the implementation of data 
driven mindset could have a significant effect on making trust in the data. It was also discovered 
from the interviews that experienced people with related data analytics, and statistics get more 
comfortable with data-driven decision-making and better data assimilation. The CFO with an IT 
background and 20 years of experience stated: 
“I think I have good analytical skills when I can relatively quick see the big picture, without 
getting into all the details.  “

4.1.4.2 Personality characteristics 
According to further research, the decision-makers' characteristics have a direct effect on 
data-driven decision-making. ( (Francioni, Musso and Cioppi 2015), ( Glinska-Newes, et al. 2020) 
(Levin and Datnow 2012) (E. Mandinach, et al. 2008)). As illustrated in Table 20, personal 
characteristics such as Need for achievement, Risk attitude, Socio-demographic characteristics 
focus on years of experiences, educational background, and Competencies focus on DDDM 
perceptions affect decision-makers approaches. 
It was identified from the interviews that decision-makers are willing to learn analytic skills, 
change their cognitive style, and make better decisions using data. For example, the Customer 
experience manager stated: 
“  I have just done another Coursera course on data analytics, artificial intelligence, so 
I'm in general interested in, in how statistics works, how data works..” 
The interviewees stated that all projects and decisions start first by looking at data, 
available facts, and the timeline for the decision. The most exciting finding is that they used data 
as support for their intuition-based decision-making. It refers to confirmation bias. Especially 
when they doubt their decision, they used data to defend their gut-feeling decisions. It shows that 
they already have the mindset to be data driven, but they need to have a structured plan to adopt 
to DDDM. They need some fundamentals such as leading, skills, people, intelligent processes, and 
availability of qualified data to perform DDDM. The Head of intelligence stated: 
“ I am using data analysis as a support for my gut feeling. So supporting or validating that, 
and sometimes you get the validation and sometimes you can get more validation that the data has 
to be more better or the analysis has to be more better and sharper. “ 
Table 20 lists the open and axial coding of personality characteristics. Again, it was noticed 
that socio-demographic specifications such as background education and experience in different 
positions significantly impact DDDM. Different positions equal to increase the knowledge. 
Knowledge has a significant influence on DDDM; As increased knowledge, decision-makers have 
more willingness to make experience-based decisions than data-driven decisions. Based on the 
interviews, most of the interviewees confirmed that there will always be gut feeling in any 
decision-making, and it comes from the knowledge achievement. For example, the Head of 
intelligence stated: 
==PAGE:74==
 
63 
 
“Knowledge is defined by the gut feeling …. deciding always complimented the gut feeling, 
plus the facts, and it depends on different leaders, how much they use the percentages to make the 
outcome or the decision ” 
Background education has a significant influence on decision-making approaches. 
Decision-makers with business and IT backgrounds have more willingness to switch to a data-
driven decision-making style.

The interviews showed that most interviewees are willing to take the risk to obtain the KPIs. 
However, they need support for taking the risk from data analytics and experienced people. 
Especially when they need to make an un-programmed decision, which consists of many unknown 
facts, it needs to be riskier than a programmed decision. The Head of Service Solution 
Development stated that they learn from their failure and adapting reasonably fast:  
“with digital solutions in the manufacturing companies so it's always a lot of unknowns, 
and of course if it's something completely new, you take risk and. And often you you fail, it's 
important to recover fast.” 
==PAGE:75==
 
64 
 
Nevertheless, they used data-driven decision-making when they doubted their gut feeling 
decision to bail out from a worst-case scenario. For example, the Vice President Product 
Development and Supply Chain mentioned: 
“…first thing I would do is I would challenge the data to get behind if there's any flaws in 
how they got the data or analyze the data. I would need to be convinced to overrule my stomach 
feeling ..And I might go for the data driven then in the end…” 
  
This study found that the dynamic environment of the manufacturing company needs to 
consider another dimension, which is uncertainty. Hence, many interviewees are forced to consider 
a specific level of uncertainty in their position as responsibility. This factor comes from unqualified 
data and finally avoid trusting to collected data. Therefore, uncertainty made decision-makers 
overrule the data-driven decision-making approaches and trust more to their experienced-based 
decisions. Therefore, the primary factor influencing decision-makers to adopt to use data-driven 
decision-making is to trust data.  
The interviews showed that as the experiences grow up, the need for data interpretation 
decrease. 
“the more experienced you get, the more gut feeling, you also get, I think for me as when I 
was a young finance person. Then, I was trying to really get to, to the 100% … I think you need to 
have done it before, to also learn it, but I think you get to a point where you say okay but now I 
have enough facts to take a decision…. I think I have good analytical skills when I can relatively 
quick see the big picture,.…”

4.1.4.3 Culture 
This study found that all interviewees are willing to change to data-driven decision-making 
and positively impression data. Nevertheless, due to the unqualified and unreliability of data, some 
prefer to make decisions by their gut feeling. To provide trust in data and qualified data, it is vital 
to improving the culture of DDDM at all levels of the organization. Therefore, it is essential to 
change the culture and mindset of the people to be more data-driven. The interviews showed that 
the interviewees referred to this problem as the leadership skills and relationship between the 
people.  
“ relations and good leadership could help people to just improve their skills for decision 
making.” 
The head of the Business intelligence stated that they developed a bottom-up community 
rather than a top-down one. Management has decided that the employees should go to the course 
to invite people to join. This helps people feel from inside that they want to learn and are ready for 
data-driven culture. He stated: 
“ I would say surprising results in the positive way….people joined the platform and we 
did learning workshops and hackathons, where people participated on their own… I think that was 
==PAGE:77==
 
66 
 
exactly to have the multi dimensional way to focus on the data driven culture. On one side we do 
the pilots, more specific use cases on the other side we generate this ideation across the company. 
And then also the people who are mostly not open to technology. You know this curve of innovation 
that laggards are the ones who are on the extreme right hand side right and the early adopters and 
the late majority.” 
As illustrated in Table 22, this study found, implementing the data-driven mindset needs 
the support and collaboration of all people at all levels of the organization. They need skilled 
people. On the other hand, they need support from the whole people involved in inputting data, 
creating insights, and usable knowledge from data. The strategy director stated: 
“..I'm also only one person lied so I can't, can't build the whole model of the world, so I'll 
need to find the areas where we're doing a project, and then have the right people to support me 
in my case..”

4.2 Summary of Data Analysis 
Analyzing the results started with face-to-face interviews with the ten (10) decision-makers 
of the climate solutions department in Danfoss. Regarding the findings in literature in chapter 2, 
the essential elements of the existing frameworks were categorized into four dimensions: Data, 
Process, Implementation, and People. The questions of the interview design were based on these 
four dimensions. After completing the interviews, the keywords and identified observations were 
extracted as main dimensions, elements, and sub-elements.  
During the interviews, the critical lacks were found out, which leads to discovers new 
insights into the lack of the current situation of data-driven approaches in the case study. 
- 
It was discovered from the analysis that experience made knowledge, and knowledge 
directly relates to intuition-based decisions. Hence, by growing up, the years of experience, 
interpreting the data and information decreased. This confirmed that experience as a 
personal factor could overrule the data-driven decision-making approaches. 
==PAGE:78==
 
67 
 
- 
Data seems to be a tool to justify intuition-based decisions. It was discovered from 
interviewees that they used data to fill the gaps of their experiences and support their 
decisions. Hence, the most common approach in the company is based on experiences. 
- 
The lack of transparency on the generation of data for decision-makers made them do not 
trust the data. 
- 
The unqualified data and unavailability of data lead decision-makers to do not trust the 
data. 
- 
Some of the decision-makers' lack of data literacy made them not understand the meaning 
of the data or use the wrong analytic method, leading to complaints as unqualified data. 
- 
It was discovered from the interviews that people with related background education such 
as business and information systems are more comfortable adopting and using data-
driven approaches for their daily activities. 
- 
Lack of system integration made to wasting time and cost to produced same analytics 
report in different departments.  
- 
Unavailability and time were two critical factors that made decision-makers not use data-
driven approaches in their decision-making processes. 
- 
The lack of a structured plan for changing the organization's culture to the data-driven 
approaches leads decision-makers to not trust the data as a robust fact for their decision-
making processes. 
- 
Lack of a structured plan for training people based on their position and need to use the 
BI tools leads them to manual calculations and used non-data-driven approaches. 
- 
The organization's hierarchical structure made those highly experienced people who are 
intuition-based decision-makers be the owner of the decisions. 
- 
Lack of strategic approaches for collecting data. 
It was noticed from this study that some items were repeated in all dimensions as weaknesses. 
These weaknesses were: Trust in data, unavailability of data, unqualified data, and data-driven 
culture. This shows that all these dimensions are interconnected, and the challenges in one 
dimension could affect the processes of the other dimensions. 
 The identified factors and findings will be discussed in the next chapter, and the 
recommendation and generated framework will be introduced. 
 
==PAGE:79==
 
68 
 
CHAPTER 5 
5 Discussion 
CHAPTER INTRODUCTION 
In this chapter, the finding of the analysis of the collected data will be discussed. The 
chapter consists of: Section 5.1 Discussion; Section 5.2 final solution; 5.3 research limitation; 5.4 
Conclusion. 
 
5.1 Discussion 
The penetration of data in organizations as a powerful business tool increasing in volume, 
variety, and size every day has led managers and decision-makers to reconsider their decision-
making methods. At the same time, the complexity and change in the data sources and decision-
making processes have increased the factors affecting the success of decisions and ultimately 
increased the productivity of companies and the closeness of competition between competitors. 
But data, as powerful as it is, can be problematic. Lack of data strategy in collecting the required 
data will lead to wasted resources and create costs. Furthermore, the existence of close competition 
between companies has also led to change in decision-making methods. Base on the finding of this 
study, decisions due to the size, importance, and availability of accurate data can be risky. 
Therefore, most companies, such as manufacturing companies, have the vision to digitalize to 
make competitive advantages and improve their performance. The manufacturing sector is now 
moving towards a new industrial revolution called Industry 4.0, which means they strive to be 
data-driven. They spend millions of dollars buying the technologies, hiring data scientist people to 
implement the data-driven approaches. As introduced in the literature, much research, investigated 
==PAGE:80==
 
69 
 
in different articles to provide a model or framework for implementation of DDDM. However, the 
story is not that simple. Companies need a framework that could lead them in the path of data-
driven. In addition, they need some tools to evaluate their implementation and find the lack before 
it becomes a considerable cost.  
This study showed that the existing frameworks and models are process-based models, 
which shows the needed process for implementing DDDM. Therefore, these frameworks are 
suitable for all companies that want to start to be data-driven. However, for companies, whose 
already implemented some steps of digitalization such as technology, hiring data scientists and 
making analytics teams, producing data, and investigating developing BI tools, the story is 
different. Analyzing the current situation of the organization in the implementation of DDDM 
approaches is essential. Dunn et al. (2013) stated that the focus should be on data, technology, and 
culture in the implementation phase. (Dunn, Airola and Garrison 2013). Therefore, this thesis 
focused on answering the following research question: ”How achieve data-driven decision-
making approaches in manufacturing companies which has challenges in the implementation 
phase of data-driven approaches?”  
In this study, various issues facing decision-makers when performing DDDM were noted. 
The interviews illustrated that some similar issues directly impact using data-driven approaches in 
each dimension of data, process, implementation, and people. This analysis helps to determine the 
barriers from the decision-makers' view and why they are not motivated to use data-driven 
analytics for their decision-making process. 
The analysis of the interviews shows that the lack of availability of data and access to data 
leads to be intuition decision-making. This approach was confirmed based on the analysis of the 
collected data in the case study of Danfoss. The interviews show that the typical approach of the 
decision-makers is still intuition-based decisions. Furthermore, it was discovered in this study that 
the essence of the department and the personality characteristics of the decision-makers have a 
significant effect on the decision-making approaches. The essence of some departments is data-
driven, such as finance, business, and strategy. However, in some departments, the unavailability 
of qualified data avoids implementing data-driven decision-making. Nevertheless, most decision-
makers stated that they would use it for their decision-making if they have access to qualified and 
reliable data. This shows they are willing to switch to a data-driven system, and they did not resist 
using the analytics reports but need a structured plan for switching to data-driven approaches.  
==PAGE:81==
 
70 
 
This research also discovered that the organization's structure has a critical effect on data-
driven decision-making. It was noticed that Danfoss has a hierarchical structure and has many 
routes for decision-making. However, decision-makers with a high level of experience are still the 
principal owners of the decisions. It was discovered that the data-driven decision-makers could 
convince the intuition-decision makers based on the solid argument on the data-driven reports and 
fill their gaps of experiences with data. Hence, the final decision will be based on data. Another 
identified factor was the size of the decisions. In decisions, which need more investigation of 
resources, they prefer to trust their experiences. This approach confirmed that lack of trust in the 
data has a significant effect on decision-making approaches. 
It was noticed during the analysis that the first and foremost problem repeated in all 
dimensions as a significant problem is lack of trust in data. Decision-makers stated that there is 
not enough transparency on the generation of the data. It seems that they do not trust their 
subordinates’ competencies. They stated that there is no system to check if the data already inputted 
in the system is in the correct format. It was identified from the literature that in the implementation 
of any digitalization system, the most challenging part is using data. Provost and Fawcett (2013) 
and Mandinach (2012) proposed that one of the essential components of the implementation of 
DDDM is the Human side. People are complicated, and organizations have natural friction points 
that make it more difficult to accept the data. This approach refers to the data literacy abilities and 
overall personal interest in the data-driven system. It is clarified that when people are not 
familiarized with new technology, they prefer to use their traditional method for performing their 
tasks. This is the same story for using data and trust in it. 
There is a need for a strategic plan to train people involved in any step of the 
implementation process, based on the need and the roles, to know how they should use data. It is 
an essential to make the expectation of producing accurate data, using the data, and considering it 
as the main factor in data strategy.  Robert Ugarte, in his book, stated that each data strategy has 
three main Dimensions: People refers to who is the users of the data. This dimension is the 
foundation. Process refers to how teams used the produced data to find valuable insights, and 
Providers refer to the tools (Ugarte 2021). He stated that most companies start with providers; 
however, that is a big mistake. Ugarte stated that the people dimension is the most important one, 
and that is where most companies run to challenges. (Ugarte 2021) 
==PAGE:82==
 
71 
 
The second most voted problem in almost all dimensions of the analysis was unqualified 
data in terms of accurate data, leading that decision-makers stated that data is not good enough or 
suitable for their decision-making processes. This issue could consider as a reason for the lack of 
trust in data in the above section. It was discovered that several factors lead to unqualified data—
architecture of the data modeling identified as an important area of improvement. As discussed in 
the literature, Bharadwaj et al. (2013) stated that a strategy for the data life cycle is essential. It 
was identified that Danfoss has different sources of collecting data such as IoTs, CRM systems, 
external data sources… and they have a considerable task on cleaning and organizing collected 
data from forty (40) years ago. The interviews showed that decision-makers need to approach 
cleaning and normalizing data to improve the data quality. As illustrated in Figure 1, Danfoss is in 
the third place of big data challenges: Veracity refers to the quality, reliability, and uncertainty in 
data. Decision-makers need to understand the meaning and the concept of the generated data to 
know where the best place is for using it in their analytics.  
Another factor that leads to unqualified data is integration. It was discovered that decision-
makers experienced that lack of access to data leads to intuition decisions. This has a significant 
effect when they have limited time. Therefore, they do not have enough time to find data and use 
it for their analysis and conclusions. On the other hand, it is noticed that lack of integrity leads to 
wasting time and money and decreases the accessibility to data. 
It was discovered in the study that increasing the amount of data and lack of integration 
leads to duplicate efforts. For example, decision-makers experienced that they spend many days 
analyzing and produced a report. Then they found out the same report was existing in another 
department. They also experienced that they do not have access to created data or analysis from 
other departments. However, the limitation of time does not let them go and find the correct data 
or reports. It was discovered that they prefer to access data and report without much effort to find 
it. Troisi (2020), in his model of the data life cycle, stated that integration should be done after the 
extraction of knowledge from data. His model of data life cycle consists of: 1) collection; 2) 
organization; 3) extraction; 4) integration; 5) analysis; 6) sharing; 7) storage; 8) reuse. (Troisi, et 
al. 2020).  
The 6th step of the Troisi model is sharing. Based on the interviews, it was discovered that 
decision-makers have experienced that they were looking for data, and it took time to find it, and 
sometimes due to the time pressure, they performed their decision based on gut feeling. This shows 
==PAGE:83==
 
72 
 
a lack of process approaches to determine how the decision-makers prefer to consume and share 
data.  
It was discovered from the analysis that the demand for data is different; some people need 
access to raw data; however, others need access to the analysis results. These needs should be 
addressed in data strategy and consider how people could feedback on data collaboratively. Troisi, 
in his article, stated that monitoring and controlling processes help to improve the quality. A 
feedback system achieved it. Furthermore, he stated that feedback produced new knowledge that 
can be used for re-used and accumulated experience for redesigning processes. (Troisi, et al. 2020).  
The interviews showed that they have some social platforms such as forums, community, 
and Microsoft Teams meeting that people could talk about their problems. However, it was noticed 
that not all interviewees were aware of these meetings. As Intezari and Gressel stated, a knowledge 
management system could help save all the best practices, including a definition for essential key 
performance indicators as a centralized location where all people have access and could add their 
suggestions for future improvements (Intezari and Gressel 2015).  
In addition, it was noticed that there are local meetings in each department or based on the 
project to reevaluate the challenges and the projects. This approach could help to find a solution 
for identified challenges. The same approach could be used for leaders of the organization to 
identify the challenges of implementing a data-driven system. Then, leaders of the organization 
can encourage other people to switch to the new system. 
During the study, decision-makers believe that knowledge comes from experience always 
involved in any decision as a gut feeling.  The point is how much they could separate gut feeling 
from the data or facts. A robust knowledge management system could control this issue. 
Furthermore, a knowledge and sharing system could help decision-makers better understand the 
effectiveness of data-driven decision-making. As mentioned before, the most common approach 
for decision-making is intuition-based decision. Converting the experiences of decision-making 
based on data or intuition and evaluate them based on the effectiveness and sharing it in knowledge 
management (KM) systems could encourage decision-makers to DDDM approaches. As Intezari 
and Gressel (2015) stated in their article, Advanced knowledge systems related to a particular sort 
of KM system help an organization incorporate big data into its repository of information and 
knowledge.  
==PAGE:84==
 
73 
 
One of the concerns of the interviewees was the relocation of employees and their lack of 
longevity. However, this issue could be controlled with the KM system. A robust KM system can 
allow new employees to access information about what happened before and the current process. 
Thus, it could prevent repetitive afford and keep all people on the same page. 
As Ugarte stated, the foundation of a data strategy is people (Ugarte 2021). Therefore, one 
dimension of investigation of this study was on people. This study identified that personal 
characteristics, data literacy, and culture significantly affect implementing the data-driven 
approaches. The lack of comprehension of the data in a business environment, lack of fundamental 
statistical skills, and lack of understanding of the domain-related data are the reason for the doubt 
in data-driven analytics reports. In the data interpretation aspect, the interviews showed that some 
users who provide the reports for decision-makers misunderstand the meaning of data or the tools 
for producing the reports. Lack of understanding of the analysis concepts in data collection and 
preparation of reports leads to doubts in decision-makers about collected data. This issue 
confirmed the idea of Levin and Datnow (2012) characterize a literate data decision-maker as 
someone who can: 1) consider the purpose of data, 2) distinguish good and bad data, 3) understand 
mathematical and calculation principles, 4) prioritize interpretation, and 5) give priority to the use 
of information, reporting and audiences. (Levin and Datnow 2012).  Sharma et al. (2014) argued 
that converting insights to decision directly relates to decision-making, and understanding insights 
achievement is vital for understanding how business analytics could perform efficiently. 
Furthermore, decision-makers emphasize that understanding the concept and the meaning 
of data and analytics tools are vital for making reliability. This issue leads the decision-makers not 
to trust the data, analysis, and subordinate competencies. This weakness in subordinate 
competencies is since they are not trained perfectly to improve their data interpretation skills. 
Therefore, the decision-makers prefer to use their experience for making decisions.  
This study identified from the analysis that personal characteristics such as Need for 
achievement, Risk attitude, Socio-demographic characteristics focus on years of experiences, 
educational background, and competencies such as data-driven decision-making perceptions affect 
decision-makers approaches.  For example, the decision-makers with related business and data 
analytics backgrounds have more motivation to use data-driven decision-making.  
 Although intuition is still a significant component in decision-making, the uncertainty of 
the environment forces the decision-makers to consider data-driven reports and analyses for their 
==PAGE:85==
 
74 
 
decision-making processes. They have the willingness to use analytics reports to fill the gaps of 
their experience or confirm them. This study shows that decision-makers without any analytic 
background education, performing self-study to improving their data literacy skills.  
It was discovered during the analysis, gaining more experience made decision-makers 
accept the high risks. They stated that in un-programmed decisions, they use the data analytics 
reports to evaluate the risk rate and need the data-driven reports to support their intuition-based 
decisions. During the study, it is identified that decision-makers' competencies significantly affect 
their decision-making approaches. It is noticed that most of the decisions are structured. Both data-
driven and intuition-decision makers confirmed that by obtaining more experience, the need for 
data interpretation decreased. It is due to the increase of knowledge, which leads them to see the 
big picture without checking all analytics reports. 
Other practices of experienced DMs include the argumentation for the correctness of 
intuition-based choices by challenging data analytics reports. As mentioned before, they use data 
analytics reports to support their intuition-based decisions. Especially when they want to measure 
the effectiveness of the risk or evaluate the effectiveness of their decisions; on the other side, when 
they doubt their decisions, they used data-driven approaches to safeguard choices when something 
goes wrong. Although the first can be seen as acceptable since the data at least are reviewed to 
verify that choices are taken with correctness. The second approach does not suggest that data-
driven decision-making is beneficial and leads to overrule the data-driven approaches. Moreover, 
if the decision failed, this approach leads to emphasis in the mindset of intuition decision-makers 
that data is not trustable.  
It is critical to improving the DDDM culture at all levels of the business to give trust in 
data and quality of data. As a result, it is critical to shift people's attitudes and mindsets to become 
more data-driven. The interviews addressed that they attribute this difficulty to leadership abilities 
and interpersonal relationships. Culture could be dividing into the personal culture and 
organizational culture. Collectivism and individualism character of decision-makers have an 
impact on the decision-making approaches. Collectivist personality leads decision-makers to put 
more weight on the more voted decision approach. As noticed before, experience-based decisions 
are still a dominating factor in decision-making. Most of the higher managers who are the owners 
of the decisions are experienced people with intuition-based decision-making approaches. It was 
discovered that collectivist characteristics lead the decision-makers to groupthink, leading to 
==PAGE:86==
 
75 
 
intuition-decision making. This discovery is in contrast with Yates and Oliveira's (2016) 
methodology. These researchers stated that collectivist culture is more likely to data-driven 
approaches by distributing the responsibility to the team. However, when the dominant approach 
for decision-making is intuition, collectivism or individualism does not affect decision-making 
processes. If the fundamentals of implementing data-driven approaches are not ready, collectivism 
could work on the opposite side and leads to resistance against data-driven implementation. 
The interviews showed that they did not have a structure change management plan for 
implementing the culture of data-driven approaches. Having a structured plan for training people 
to learn how to use data and tools could close the gaps when companies start to be data-driven. 
Some people, who understand the meaning of data and analysis and are responsible for providing 
the tools and analytics reports, discovered that some people do not understand data and analysis.  
It was discovered that they have some training for the rest employees when launching tools. 
However, the IT and analysis department experienced that some people used the wrong tools or 
analytic methods. It shows that the training was not based on the needs of the employees, or the 
training was a long time before they needed it and led to forgot it.  
In this study, it was discovered that when all team members are participating in developing 
a tool for producing an analytic report, all team members could use it, and they do not have any 
problem related to the meaning of the method or data. This discovery confirmed that having a 
knowledge system that all employees and decision-makers have access to it, can present their 
suggestions for developing any process related to their needs is essential.  KM system helps the 
growth of the data-driven culture align with data strategy and keeps all users of the new system on 
the same page. 
 This is very common; data experts assume that people will learn over time. (Ugarte 2021). 
The most complex challenge in implementing data-driven approaches is using data. It is related 
directly to people issues such as lack of trust, lack of data literacy skills, and time to learn new 
skills for using BI tools. Ugarte discovered that companies come to these positions because they 
have excellent technical people enthusiastic about data. However, due to the lack of a strategic 
plan for change management, they cannot convince the rest of their organization to match their 
enthusiasm or expertise (Ugarte 2021). The interviews identified that when a new tool launched, 
they have training for all people, and it was not customized based on their needs and technical 
ability. Therefore, the training could be considered valuable, tedious, or complex. Therefore, it is 
==PAGE:87==
 
76 
 
not far from the mind that they will forget them until they need to use them. Ugarte suggested that 
training should be an ongoing process and should never stop. He proposed that, over time, greater 
emphasis be placed on ad hoc, reactive, and documentation training alternatives and controlling 
how much time individuals spend with data (Ugarte 2021). 
Finally, based on the finding of this study, these challenges and benefits of implementing 
a DDDM approach were identified. The biggest challenges of implementing data-driven 
approaches are consists of :  
• Make more transparency on data 
• Availability of qualified and reliable data 
• Integration 
• Adopting people by training, developing knowledge system 
• Improving the data management and data modeling approaches 
The benefits of implementing data-driven approaches are: 
• Improving the quality of decision to be more objective and informed 
• Fast decision-making with high performance. 
• Create collaboration. 
• Creating effective competitive advantages 
 
The summarization of the findings of the challenges in each dimension and recommendations is 
given in Table 23.

• 
Improve the quality of the reports and analytics to make sense 
for decision-makers and look more reliable. 
 
• 
Developing a structured strategy for training people to improve 
their competency and data literacy skills. Ugarte recommended 
designing the training around four blocks: Group, individual, 
reactive, and documentation (Ugarte 2021). It is essential to start 
training people on what they need to know to start. Then buy 
individual and reactive support, their skills will improve. One of 
the practical approaches is using ADKAR, which refers to 
awareness, Desire, Knowledge, Ability, and Reinforcement. 
 
• 
It is recommended to keep training as an ongoing process and 
never stop. 
 
 
All these identified challenges and recommendations are related naturally and affect each 
other. There is a need for a strategic plan to align the data strategy with the business goal. As 
discussed in the literature, data must fulfill a company's strategic imperatives (Saxena 2019). 
Collecting data does not make value. As discussed in chapter 2, it is crucial to have an approach 
==PAGE:89==
 
78 
 
for collecting data. For instance, how does data lead to generating value? How to govern data in 
an organization? What is the plan for the data life cycle? (Ugarte 2021) 
A data strategy's role is to define the targets and help the companies make competitive 
advantages by making value. Value is the result of the business processes and comes from a 
strategic business plan. Therefore, prioritizing the projects based on the available data and making 
the evidence to show how much value in the sense of revenue or reducing the cost is produced 
could encourage the decision-makers to have more trust in data.  
To improve processes, it was recommended to implement a robust knowledge management 
system that all people have access to and could insert their suggestions. For example, in the data 
analysis chapter, it was mentioned by the interviewees, when all team members were involved in 
the process of developing a tool or an analytic report, then all of them understand and learn the 
meaning of tools and produced data and analytic reports. So, they are all motivated to use the 
developed tools for their daily activities. This approach could be expanded as a knowledge 
management system for all employees to involve them in developing or improving BI tools. 
 However, the benefits of a knowledge management system are for all dimensions. For 
instance, people could find updated information about the implementation of data-driven 
approaches; They could learn from the experience of others about using the BI tools to find a 
solution for their issues during the using the analytics tools; They could read the successful 
experiences of using data in the decision-making process; they could be aware of the reason for 
the failure in decisions and learn from it, involvement in developing the processes could help them 
to understand the meaning of produced data developed tools which leads to growth in the data 
mindset. All these examples are related to other dimensions and could be collected in the 
knowledge system. Therefore, A Knowledge management system could be used as a general 
solution for all dimensions and help to improve them.  
In the implementation dimension, it was recommended to have a strategic change 
management plan. Of course, all these suggestions affect data strategy too. For example, it was 
described in chapter 2 that the first step of implementing a data strategic road map is about people 
(Ugarte 2021). It was also stated in Saxena’s data strategy road map that the first step was to 
educate people to have a common understanding of the process and keep them on the same page 
==PAGE:90==
 
79 
 
regarding the implementation of data-driven approaches (Saxena 2019). A structured change 
management plan helps people be aware of the goals of the DDDM approach and their roles in the 
implementation and make desire in them. Furthermore, with a structured training plan, the 
analytics skills of employees and decision-makers will improve. All these strategies lead to 
improve the data mindset in the organization.  Therefore, all these identified challenges and 
recommended solutions are the dots of the data-driven approaches and interconnected to gather. 
Any improvement in one dimension has a significant effect on the other dimensions. 
It was recommended in the people dimension to improve decision-makers' analytic skills 
by developing some measurement tools and a strategic training plan. Developing a measurement 
tool for evaluating the effectiveness of the new tools and making a comparison with traditional 
tools could help decision-makers trust the tools and analytics reports. For instance, Ugarte (2021), 
in his book, proposed this formula for measuring the value per tool :  
 
 
Another helpful tool is defining the key decision processes and redesigning themes based 
on data-driven approaches. For instance, “Intellishore.dk “ is a company investigated in defining 
the tools for implementing data-driven decision making.  As illustrated in Figure 15, They 
proposed a tool for redesigning the critical decision-making processes. The first step in this tool is 
defining the users. Next is the process, the identified users involved in what kind of processes. The 
third step shows the current output, and the fourth step illustrated the expected future 
improvement—finally, in Dashboard, an overview of the available tools and data.
