Figure 15: Redesigning Key Decision Processes ( Source:https://intellishore.dk ) 
Another recommended approach for redesigning the processes is Gap analysis.  Sharma 
stated that gap analysis is a technique to define the current state of the actual performance and 
expected performance (A. Sharma 2013). This technique could define the shortcomings to 
overcome in processes, products, sales services, or any other operation. The main steps in this 
method are defining the focus areas, the current state, what is expected future state, identifying 
gaps that could be lack in data, in tools, in user skills, and finally, an action plan that refers to any 
solution to bridge the gaps.  
In the implementation dimension, an example of tools could be the data governance 
maturity assessment proposed by “Intellishore.dk”.  This tool helps to identify the critical issues 
in data governance. ( See Figure 16 ) 
==PAGE:92==
 
81 
 
 
Figure 16: Data Governance Maturity Assessment ( Source: https://intellishore.dk) 
 
In People, dimension recommended developing a strategy for training people for 
improving their competency and skills.  The recommended tool ADKAR could cover the goals 
of the change management strategy. Because all employees need to improve their skills, 
organizational behavior, and culture align with the data-driven strategy.  It was discovered during 
the study that training should be based on the needs of the employees and their current 
competency or personal skills. Two valuable tools for Measuring Team Skills -proposed by 
Ugarte – and Competency Gap Analysis – proposed by “Intellishore.dk”.   
Ugarte (2021) stated that the first step in people strategy is to assess the team skills 
consist of:  technical expertise; statistical skills; business strategy refer to align their work with 
business strategy; using tools refers to how their feeling by employing the existing tools for their 
daily activities; and decision-making abilities (Ugarte 2021). He proposed measure team skills 
(MTS). ( See Figure 17 ) 
==PAGE:93==
 
82 
 
 
Figure 17: The MTS assessment helps to understand the team's skill makeup (Source: (Ugarte 2021)) 
 The second tool for analyzing the Competency gaps is classifying the currently available 
competencies and critical skill gaps. This tool helps to identify the gaps of competencies in 
departments. As illustrated in Figure 18, this tool is such an enabler to find the improvement areas 
in each department.  
 
Figure 18:Competency gap analysis ( Source: https://intellishore.dk) 
==PAGE:94==
 
83 
 
For implementing strategic change management, defining the skills and competencies 
leads to planning the needed training for the employees and avoiding wasting time and money on 
training that employees already know. Furthermore, based on the data analysis, it was discovered 
that employees are motivated to learn new tools. Therefore, by planning targeted training, these 
potentials can be purposefully expanded in line with business goals. 
 
5.2 Final Solution 
  
As mentioned before, this study aimed to propose a framework for companies which 
already implemented their infrastructures; they are producing data, proactive insights and using 
them for their analysis, but were not entirely successful in implementing data-driven decision-
making.  
 Based on the findings in section 1.4 and data analysis in chapter 4, it is clear that Danfoss 
is in the implementation phase and has trouble using data-driven approaches for decision-making 
processes. Therefore, they need a framework to adapt their decision-makers to data-driven 
approaches. As illustrated in Figure 19, this study proposed a framework for finding a better 
solution for any company such as Danfoss, which is struggled in the implementation phase. 
When companies implemented data-driven systems, this framework could be considered 
as an optimization tool for them. Therefore, the focus of this framework is suggesting the tools 
that help find a solution for the most common challenges during the implementation phase in data-
driven approaches. Based on the literature, most of these challenges are popular among companies 
and related to technology, culture and data( (Provost and Fawcett 2013), (Dunn, Airola and 
Garrison 2013), (Sharma, Mithas and Kankanhalli 2014), (Ugarte 2021), (Saxena 2019)). 
 
==PAGE:95==
 
84 
 
 
Figure 19:Proposed framework for dealing with challenges in the implementation phase of data-driven 
decision making 
The proposed framework consists of four dimensions – Data, Process, Implementation, 
People- related to improvement, adopting, and influencing decision-makers for using data-driven 
approaches in their decision-making processes. For applying this framework, the first step is to 
identify the organization's current situation in implementing data-driven decision-making.  
  The organization must evaluate the current state of the implementation and define the 
challenges. They need to define the challenges where people are not comfortable working with 
tools and data. These challenges could be related to the tools, data, or people. The challenges could 
be investigated by using the interview questions presented in Appendix 3: Interview Questions. 
The interview questions of this study are open questions and more general. These questions could 
be used for any other company to identify the current state of their implementation.  As explained 
in section 3.3 Questioner Design and Interviewees Profiles, the questions are based on four 
identified dimensions. However, the organization can customize them based on their needs. Based 
==PAGE:96==
 
85 
 
on the results of the questions, organizations could be identified in which dimension they have 
problems and use the suggested solution in that dimension. Therefore, the proposed framework 
could be used partly or wholly based on the identified lacks in the implementation phase.  
5.2.1 Data 
Data dimension focuses on defining a precise data strategy and aligning them with business 
goals.  Based on the increasing amount of data every day, finding the best approach for collecting 
and preparing needed raw data as structured data for processes is essential. It is recommended to 
investigate the project that already has reliable data and create qualified reports and analytic tools 
to make evidence for decision-makers to trust the availability of qualified data. A qualified data 
strategy leads to prepares the foundation of trust into data for any users and decision-makers. Based 
on the discussion in the previous section that data strategy affects all other dimensions. If data 
strategy aligns with the business goal, it is easier to prioritize the tasks of the data life cycle – data 
architecture, normalizing, cleaning- based on the high-value projects. Furthermore, this approach 
leads to make reliable analytics reports for decision-makers to feel more confident on data.  
Therefore, it is essential to revise the data strategies and assess how much they align with the 
business strategy. One of the proper tools that could help assess data strategy implementation is 
illustrated in Figure 25: Tool’s assessment Criteria (See Appendices 2: More tools for 
implementation). This tool helps to see if the strategies are executed as planned.   
Companies could also design their tools for evaluating the effectiveness of the data strategy. 
For example, Ugarte (2021) suggested some questions for developing the right metrics for 
measuring the success along the way of implementing data strategy, which consists of: 
- 
Is the implementation progress steady? For example, It might be lacking in training or 
internal support. 
- 
Is the Data accurate (in any amount)? Ugarte suggested that having limited but accurate 
data is better than having a large amount of unqualified data. 
- 
Are people using the data in their day-to-day lives and meeting? For example, it could be 
identified by looking at the reports and presentations in meetings that how much of them 
are based on data. 
==PAGE:97==
 
86 
 
- 
Is the organization progressing in analytics maturity? For example, by measuring the 
growth rate of analytics skills in change management strategy, it is possible to see how 
much they executed as they planned.  
5.2.2 Process 
The next dimension, namely Process. It is essential to have a strong knowledge 
management system accessible for all people and decision-makers to share their suggestions or 
experiences for improvement in developing the processes, as explained in the above section. 
Knowledge management systems have the potential to improve in all dimensions simultaneously. 
In general view, A knowledge management system could help people learn from each other's 
experiences; it helps that people feel their suggestion is essential for improving the processes and 
feel more responsible for participation, which indirectly develops a data-driven mindset.  
Development in data-driven mindsets motivates the employees to participate in change 
management programs more actively and believe in the benefits of data and trust in analytic tools. 
Another advantage of the knowledge system is for newly hired decision-makers; they could find 
all previous practices for designing the available tools. 
It is also recommended to develop measurement tools for evaluating the effectiveness of 
the tools. The evaluation helps to identify how much they are aligned with the strategic goal. One 
of the valuable tools recommended to use in this dimension is redesigning key decision processes. 
As illustrated in Figure 15: Redesigning Key Decision Processes ( Source:https://intellishore.dk ), 
this tool helps to presents the expected future improvement in the processes, defines the users and 
the current output, and the expected output for the future. Most of the expected future output could 
be identified based on the data strategy in the Data dimension and the results from the knowledge 
management system. Therefore, the data scientists could identify the needs and expectations of the 
tools and consider them for future improvement and redesigning the processes. 
The other tool used in the process dimension to evaluate the tool's effectiveness is 
illustrated in Figure 14 value per insight suggested by Ugarte (2021). This tool can also make 
evidence for decision-makers in the Data dimension to see how valuable the BI tools are by 
improving the revenue or reducing the costs.  
==PAGE:98==
 
87 
 
5.2.3 Implementation 
The Third dimension, Implementation, is the most critical. The focus of this dimension is 
on changing the culture of the organization based on the strategic plan. It is the company's general 
mistake when implementing data-driven approaches; the most focus is on designing the tools and 
technology. However, as mentioned in previous sections, the most challenging part is using the 
tools and data. Hence, changing the organization's culture is a process that should be started from 
the first step of implementing the new system (Ugarte 2021). 
Culture is frequently linked to a particular leader or leadership team; most of the procedures 
could design and construct by leaders who drive the change. Furthermore, the change strategy 
should consider both the psychological needs and the users' needed data literacy, directly affecting 
the people dimension. As shown in Figure 19, some hints are recommended. First, getting everyone 
on board helps to analyze a process from many views—this helps to engage everyone who is the 
direct or indirect user of the process to make their suggestion and be aware of the benefits of the 
outputs of the designed tools.  Ugarte (2021) stated that Engineer teams, legal or compliance teams, 
Marketing teams, product teams, sales teams, management, and any other teams should be 
considered when implementing a data-driven approach.  For example, the engineering and 
technical teams are responsible for developing tools as easily as possible that make confidence in 
decision-makers to use them. Legal teams care about any issues with data, such as leaks and 
privacy laws. Marketing teams care about the costs and how they report based on data. The product 
team cares about customer satisfaction by producing better products. The sales teams care to have 
access to real-time data and deals. Hence, the sales team needs valuable data, which leads them to 
useful insights quickly. Finally, management teams care about performance. However, the 
leadership role for implementing digitalization approaches is very significant.   
The second hint is establishing the correct ownership for any implementation. By assigning 
a particular person or team to responsible for a specific task such as supporting the team for data 
adoption, the data management team is responsible for managing data and making integrity in 
produced data and make access for people, owner of the technical components, etc.  All these 
ownerships help people to know where they could address their problems during adopting data-
driven approaches. The finding of these study shows that people preferred to access to tools and 
data without many efforts. For instance, if decision-makers have struggled to find data or reports, 
==PAGE:99==
 
88 
 
they prefer to do it based on their intuition. Ugarte (2021) stated that ownership does not end when 
implementation ends. For continuous improvement, this process is ongoing and never ends. 
The third hint is transparency on data schema. By defining the data schema, it is possible 
to collect the data based on the needs of the decision-makers and users. Moreover, as identified 
from the interviews, transparency helps to trust into data.  
The fourth hint is to design appropriate budgets. Again, based on the finding of this study, 
it is recommended to start with the more valuable projects from which the sources are available. 
This approach helps people see the effectiveness of data-driven approaches, helps trust data and 
motivates them to use the new tools. Ugarte (2021) recommended being aggressive in adapting to 
new tools to reduce costs. Therefore it is essential to provide tools for measuring the success of 
the tools. One of the best tools introduced before is Figure 14: value per insight ( Source : (Ugarte 
2021)).  
Another tool illustrated in Figure 16: Data Governance Maturity Assessment ( Source: 
https://intellishore.dk) helps evaluate data governance's current state. This tool helps identify the 
essential data governance concerns to solve. In case of any defect and weaknesses, other tools 
introduced in the above sections help find the cause. Defining the causes makes it easier to 
compensate for them to prevent possible failures in other dimensions. For instance, low grades on 
the people side could be based on a lack of data literacy which could be evaluated using the 
introduced tool in Figure 24: Assessment of current skills and needs (Source: . This tool helps to 
assess the team's skills. If the results are not as expected, they need to have more focus on training 
strategies. A change management plan boosts analytical skills and boosts mental and cultural 
development, and leads the employee to apply the data-driven approach in their tasks. It is possible 
to implement a centralized change program that using cognitive technologies helps the leaders to 
identify the motivators elements in employees and sentiments them with the business goals. All 
users should feel the importance of their roles in the new system.  
Another tool that could help assess the implementation is Figure 18:Competency gap 
analysis ( Source: https://intellishore.dk).  This tool helps to assess the makeup of analytics — 
business analyst, BI project management, BI application developer, Data mining analyst— in each 
department. By combining the results of this tool and Figure 15: Redesigning Key Decision 
Processes ( Source:https://intellishore.dk ), it is possible to make more transparency on the analytic 
needs of the departments for skilled analytics employees and future improvement in their processes. 
==PAGE:100==
 
89 
 
 
5.2.4 People 
The last dimension is people. The reason for dividing the people from the organization's 
culture is that people are the users of the tools and data. Based on the finding in the literature, the 
biggest mistake companies make in implementing a data-driven approach is to think that by 
spending money on setting up the best technologies, they can easily persuade employees to switch 
to new approaches.  However, the finding of this study proves the opposite. Based on the finding 
of this study and scholarly articles discussed in the literature review, it is verified that the most 
challenging part is people. Given the identified challenges of the study, if decision-makers do not 
feel comfortable and confident with the tools and data, they will resist implementing data-driven 
decision-making. Furthermore, the decision-makers' data literacy skills and personal 
characteristics regarding years of experience, competencies, perceptions from decision-making 
processes, and risk directly affect their confidence in data-driven decision-making. Therefore, it is 
essential to improve the data literacy of the users of the data-driven approaches by training based 
on their needs and responsibilities in their positions.  
Developing a tool for evaluating the effectiveness of the decisions is essential to recognize 
and encourage decision-makers by comparing the data-driven decision and intuition decisions in 
terms of revenue, quality, duration. This helps to provide the required level of influence by making 
tangible benefits for the high-level intuition decision-makers to trust data-driven decision-making. 
The value per insight tool (Figure 14) could be used again in this dimension to evaluate the 
effectiveness of the decisions. By measuring the value of decisions based on data and comparing 
it with the value of decisions based on intuition, it is possible to clarify the benefits for decision-
makers. 
The proposed framework in the people dimension is recommended to improving the quality 
of reports. It is essential to define the audiences of the reports and choose the best visualization for 
them. Ugarte (2021), in his book, stated that it is a difference between report and data analytic 
reports; Reports are a summary of the ongoing process and findings and used as the inputs for data 
analysis processes. For instance, summarize of performance of six months ago.  However, data 
analysis is converting the raw data of reports to actionable insights (Ugarte 2021). For instance, 
==PAGE:101==
 
90 
 
the service management might be interested in digging into that data and finding out why it is not 
as expected.  
Based on the finding of this study, it was recommended to develop a structured strategy for 
training people. Assessing the technical skills of decision-makers and employees for transferring 
the identified knowledge from data to actionable insights that are understandable for the users and 
decision-makers is essential. As illustrated in Figure 17: The MTS assessment helps to understand 
the team's skill makeup (Source: (Ugarte 2021)), which helps to know how technical training is 
needed for audiences. Ugarte (2021) recommended four focus areas for training clients. First, 
Group training will be designed for each team, such as sales, marketing, production, etc., to 
introduce the basics and concepts. Second, individual training focuses on individual sessions to 
find out the challenges. Third, reactive training focuses on problems when people start to use data 
and mining for actionable insights. Finally, registering the best practices as documentation. 
One of the practical methodologies for implementing structured training and organizational 
change is ADKAR (Hiatt 2006). This model, as shown in Figure 23 (In Appendices 2: More tools 
for implementation), consists of awareness, desire, knowledge, ability, and reinforcement. The first 
two steps are for change and a communication plan. In these two steps, employees and decision-
makers will be aware of change goals and motivated to change. Thus, these two steps support the 
change management strategy in the implementation dimension.  The following two steps— 
Knowledge and ability— included the training strategy and plan, and the last step— 
Reinforcement— is for sustaining change. This model helps implement the change in culture and 
people and train them by making readiness in employees and decision-makers. This finding 
confirmed that all these dimensions are interconnected, and success in each dimension 
significantly affects the other dimension. Therefore, these dimensions support each other. 
Therefore, for better results, all dimensions should manage simultaneously. 
The continuous training support decision-makers to practice more data-driven decision-
making approaches as maturity in data-driven decision-making. Evaluating employees’ skills (See 
Figure 24), the success of the strategies implemented in training and changing employees and 
measuring the data governance capabilities (See Figure 16) helps to monitor the change and 
training progress.  
==PAGE:102==
 
91 
 
Therefore, to apply the proposed framework of this study, companies need to go through 
these three steps: 
❖ First: evaluate the current situation and defining the challenges by using the 
interview questions. 
❖ Second: Based on the identified challenges, use the suggested solution in 
dimensions. 
❖ Third: Use the introduced tools to assess and monitor the success of implementation. 
 
Figure 20: The three main steps for applying the proposed framework 
 The loop between steps two and three is an ongoing process until the implementation ends 
up successfully. Any company, by applying these three steps, could use this framework during its 
implementation phase.  
 
5.2.5 Comparison to the existing framework 
As mentioned in section 2.6 Summary of the Literature, the existing frameworks 
( (Davenport, Harris and Morison 2010) (E. Mandinach 2012) (Hall, Jia and Song 2015)) are a 
process-based model, which introduced the needed processes for implementing data-driven 
decision-making. On the other hand, the proposed model by Troisi et al. introduced how to lead 
big data through data-driven processes (Troisi, et al. 2020).  All these frameworks and models are 
suitable for companies that want to start to set up a data-driven decision-making approach. These 
models did not consider the potential challenges during the implementation and did not 
recommend any solutions or tools.  
==PAGE:103==
 
92 
 
The proposed framework aims to improve the implemented data-driven approaches in all 
dimensions. Moreover, as mentioned before, this framework can consider as an optimization tool 
besides the existing frameworks to find a solution for potential challenges during the 
implementation of data-driven approaches. Hence, there is a need first to evaluate the 
organization's current situation in implementing a data-driven approach to define the challenges 
that lead to failures in implementation, such as unreliability, non-integrity, unqualified data, 
unskilled decision-makers, etc. 
 Furthermore, with the tools introduced in section 5.1 and appendix 2, comprehensive and 
continuous monitoring can be implemented to evaluate implementing data-driven decision-making. 
  
 5.3 Research Limitation 
For this research, the following limitations can be noted. First, this study was conducted in 
the case study of Danfoss -in the climate solution department- in Denmark as one of the world's 
biggest manufacturing companies. The focus of the study was on internal value creation and how 
to encourage decision-makers to data-driven approaches. Hence, to ensure that decision-makers 
have knowledge and experience about the data-driven approaches, the study focuses on collecting 
data from key decision-makers such as managers and department heads to get reliable answers. 
Future research could consider interviewing more decision-makers from other departments to get 
a broader grasp on the data-driven decision-making process. However, the other departments could 
have different experiences and perspectives on data utilization in their decision-making processes. 
Therefore, it could help to expand this framework and improve the validity and reliability of the 
results.  
Second, designing tools for measuring the effectiveness of the decision processes, strategic 
change management plan, metrics for measuring the success of the tools are complex tasks and 
was out of focus of this study and could be an area for investigation for future study. Therefore the 
introduced tools were identified from literature researches. Companies could design other tools to 
have precise measuring on the success of implementation. Designing more practical tools can be 
another area for future researches. 
Thirdly, based on the finding of this study, people characteristics and culture have a 
significant effect on the utilization of data-driven approaches. In addition, manufacturing 
==PAGE:104==
 
93 
 
companies are different in terms of size, market share, and type. Since this study was conducted 
in Denmark, it is interesting to generalize the results in other industries with a different culture. 
Additionally, investigating family-own companies, multinational enterprises, business groups. It 
is interesting to find differences by making a distinction between companies based on the above 
specification and using them as analysis for finding a better solution for utilizing big data for 
decision-making approaches. 
 
5.4 Conclusion 
The role of data and diversity of the data and knowledge sources from inside and outside 
of organizations have increased the complexity of decision-making processes. The essence of the 
decision could make it risky and critical and relies on the size of the decision, expertise, 
experiences, perceptions, the personality of decision-makers, and expectations. Moreover, in 
modern days, the availability of data in terms of velocity, variety, volume, veracity, and value has 
a practical impact on the quality and the success of the decisions. Therefore, companies need to 
have a framework that includes all aspects of data-driven approaches for implementation. 
Therefore, this study investigated finding the barriers to implementing data-driven approaches 
from the view of decision-makers in a manufacturing company in the case of Danfoss. The 
literature reviews investigated to define the essential factors for implementing data-driven 
decision-making. Based on the findings of the literature and the existing frameworks – as 
illustrated in Table 3 - the four dimensions as most challenging areas identified: Data, Process, 
Implementation, and People. The interview questions design was based on these dimensions to 
analyze the current situation of implementing the data-driven approaches in the Danfoss-climate 
solution department. It becomes clear that the most common approach of decision-making in 
Danfoss is intuition. It is discovered that lack of trust in data, unqualified data, unavailability of 
data are the main challenges for decision-makers. 
Additionally, In the process of becoming more data-driven, this research also recognized 
difficulties. In line with the identified challenges described in the literature, the lack of data literacy 
and personal characteristics specification such as competencies, years of experiences, decision-
making perception, and risk attitude of the decision-makers have significant effects on data-driven 
decision-making. The identified benefit of data-driven decision-making in this study was: 
==PAGE:105==
 
94 
 
Improving the quality of the decisions, more objective decisions, improve the process of decision-
making, create collaboration, and create effective competitive advantages.  
For engaging the decision-makers and promotion of data-driven mindset, it was 
recommended to divide the organization's culture from the people characteristics and provide a 
separate plan for adopting its culture and people. Most companies investigate millions of dollars 
in technologies and develop modern analytics tools; with this perception, it is easy to use them for 
daily tasks and data-driven decision-making. However, this study shows that it is not correct. This 
study shows that the most challenging part is people. It was verified that without changing the 
decision-makers' behavior to data-driven approaches and developing the tools based on their needs 
and expectations, all these investigations lost time and money. It was argued that alignment 
between data strategy and business strategy is essential. It helps align divers’ teams with a shared 
understanding of defined business goals, supports business strategies, and leads to trust in data and 
analytics. 
In addition, based on the identified challenges from this study in the case study, it is verified 
that the Triosi model is the most completed model, including all aspects of the data-driven 
decision-making approaches. Therefore, this model could be used as starting approach for 
companies that want to set up digitalization. Finally, the final solution of this study was proposed 
as a framework to suggest solutions for identified challenges in each dimension of the study ( Data, 
Process, Implementation, and People). These challenges were identified based on the interviews 
and evaluate the company's current state from the decision-makers' perspective. Therefore, 
identifying the current situation of the implementation is the starting step for applying the proposed 
framework. The next step is using the suggested solution in each dimension, and the third step is 
using the tools for assessing the success of the implemented solution. It was recommended to 
continue the loop between the second and third steps until the success in implementation. 
 Therefore, this framework could be used as an optimization tool besides the other 
frameworks for improving the implementation of data-driven decision-making approaches during 
the implementation phase. In terms of practical contribution, this study provides companies with 
more minor or average experiences in the process of data-driven decision-making. Additionally, it 
highlights the importance of data literacy and analytical skills implication related to the impact of 
the data-driven on empowerment of decision-makers and employees, and how it can be integrated 
with the organization to augment.

Appendix 3: Interview Questions 
Project Description: 
Many organizations want to make value from their collected data and use it as a competitive 
advantage against the competitors. This study introduced to what extend data can contribute to 
developing decision-making. Accordingly, encouraging the decision-makers to switch from the 
intuition-based decision to DDDM is a complex process. Many factors have influenced the success 
of implementing a DDDM framework. Furthermore, the impact of decision-makers characteristic 
on big data adaption of data-driven decision making will be investigated. 
This study addresses the organization's general problem of implementing an intelligent 
framework for utilizing data in decision-making. Previous research indicates that despite the 
popularity and success of data-driven decision-making, many companies and organizations are 
still struggling to successfully implement a framework for data-driven decision-making.  
The goal of the questions:  
❖ Analyzing the current process of decision making 
❖ Find the barriers for Data-driven decision-making: The second topic was about the 
implementation of data-driven decision-making. In this part, the focus was on the 
challenges and benefits of implementation.  
❖ Find the characterize information about decision-makers. 
People Questions: 
1- Could you please explain your roles and what is your daily tasks, activities, and 
responsibilities? Educations? experiences? individualistic or collectivist personality? 
2- How much of your intuition with professional experience has affect on your decision 
making approach?Has your approach to decision-making changed with experience? 
3- Do you have any willingness to change to cognitive style? 
4- What kind of skills in terms of data literacy do you have? ( 
Data knowledge: simple understanding of statistical principles and terminology 
such as their correlation. 
Data assimilation: A simple understanding of the title, label, data source, filters, 
sorting, targets 
Interpretation: refers to analyzing and interpreting skills such as pattern, gap 
analysis, Skewness, outliers  
==PAGE:119==
 
108 
 
, skepticism, and curiosity: Decision-makers should stand back and consider other 
considerations which are less apparent, and which may influence the findings and 
their interpretation and think critically about collected data such as collection 
methods, context, comparations, bias, etc.) 
 
5- What score do you give to yourself in terms of data literacy? (1-5) 
6- What is the role of your experience with your company in the use of analysis and 
decision-making based on reports, graphs, data, etc.? 
7- How much risk are you willing to take when making decisions to achieve the target or 
set KPIs? 
8- Do you have any idea how to improve the quality of decision-making in your 
personality? 
 
Data Questions: 
1- Do you know if there is any plan or strategy for what kind of data is needed to collect 
future improvement in devices or services? 
2- Do you know what kind of infrastructures is using in Danfoss for collecting data? 
3- Do you know what kind of data you are collecting in the company?  
4- Do you have any meetings to know what kind of data is available in the company or 
any workshop for learning the analytic tools?  
5-  Had you ever looking for a specific kind of data for your analysis?  
6- Do you have any idea how to improve the quality of the data? 
7- Is there any feedback system on decisions for decision-makers?  
 
Process Questions: 
1- What is the usual decision-making approach used in your company? Is it data-driven 
or intuition-based decision-making? 
2- Have you come across situations even though analytics and reports are provided; 
still, the managers decide it based on their intuition/gut feeling? Any specific reasons 
for this? What did they do, and what did they trust to make a decision (experience or 
analysis)? 
3- Is there any feedback system to find out the effectiveness of the decisions? 
4- What could improve to enhance the quality of decision-making processes? 
 
Implementation: 
1- What does the implementation of data-driven decision-making mean for Danfoss in 
terms of challenges and benefits? 
==PAGE:120==
 
109 
 
2- Is there any control or monitoring system to measure and evaluate the effectiveness 
and outcomes of the decisions? 
3- How the learning and the produced knowledge of the outcomes of a decision can be 
share between decision-makers? 
4- What could improve to enhance the quality of implementation of data-driven 
decision-making quality? 
 
 
Thanks for participation. 
Mahsa Eskandarzadeh

Interviewee  10:29

Q: Has your approach to decision making change with your experiences? 
Interviewee  12:42

everybody access to it. So I see more people are starting to use these dashboards, and starting to base 
decision and decisions on them, and I see it, because when I, when I review, let's say, business, progress, 
sales progress. I see screen dumps of these dashboards being built into, into, presentations, and that for me 
says a nice indication that we're starting to, as a company to adopt this, but it does require that somebody 
sits down and structures the data, but we save a lot of time in the long run once we've done it because then 
when you need to build a quarterly basis report. You don't need to sit back and start collecting data and 
visualizing you can actually just rely on, on the say the central repository that we have available.

Yes, very much so.

Q: Do you know if there is any plan or strategy for what kind of data is needed to collect

Q: What does the implementation of data-driven decision-making mean for Danfoss in terms 
of challenges and benefits?  
• 
When done right, it would lead to faster decision-making as well as more quality/fact based 
decisions (i.e. reduce biases) 
• 
Challenge is when the data itself is biased or not correctly understood this would have the opposite 
effect and lead to “blind decision making” and not questioning whether it is the correct decision. It 
could potentially also lead to reducing ownership of decision and instead “blaiming” the data 
Q: Is there any control or monitoring system to measure and evaluate the effectiveness and 
outcomes of the decisions?  
• 
Current we have a quality management system where documentation for decisions are captured, i.e. 
through minutes of meetings, reports, reporting meetings etc. Furthermore dashboard include 
tracking of previous decisions as well as strategic KPIs that are being tracked (e.g. the outcome of 
decisions) 
Q: How the learning and the produced knowledge of the outcomes of a decision can be share 
between decision-makers?  
• 
Knowledge-sharing forums, regular follow-up meetings and reports 
• 
Databases capturing quality data, i.e. feedback and actions from customer meeting made readily 
available for a large and relevant workforce 
Q :What should/could improve to enhance the quality of implementation of data-driven 
decision-making quality & reaching KPIs?  
• 
Training and support functions. I.e. offering courses on data-driven decision making, statistics, data 
mgmt. etc. 
• 
Dedicated function responsible for spreading awareness and developing the needed courses 
targeting key relevant stakeholders
